**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy TLS Certificate Validation Pipeline

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement TLS certificate validation. Identify: the abstract CertValidator interface, the DefaultCertValidator with X.509 chain verification, the SAN matcher for Subject Alternative Name matching (DNS, URI, email, IP), the ContextImpl managing TLS certificates and OCSP responses, and the OCSP response parsing and stapling support.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Envoy v1.31.2 codebase and created a comprehensive `answer.json` file documenting all TLS certificate validation components.

## Summary

The analysis found **23 C++ source files** implementing the TLS certificate validation pipeline across the github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2 repository:

### Key Components Identified:

1. **Abstract CertValidator Interface** - Defines validation contract in `source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h`

2. **DefaultCertValidator** - Primary X.509 validator implementing:
   - X.509 chain verification
   - Certificate hash pinning (SHA-256)
   - SPKI pinning
   - Subject Alternative Name (SAN) verification
   - Asynchronous and synchronous validation

3. **SAN Matcher System** - `san_matcher.h/.cc` handling:
   - DNS, URI, email, IP, and OTHER_NAME SAN types
   - String matching patterns (exact, prefix, suffix, regex)

4. **ContextImpl Classes** - Manages TLS contexts:
   - `ContextImpl` base class
   - `ServerContextImpl` with OCSP stapling
   - `ClientContextImpl` for client-side validation
   - `TlsContext` struct holding certificates and OCSP responses

5. **OCSP Response Pipeline** - Complete RFC 6960 support:
   - `OcspResponseWrapperImpl` for DER-encoded responses
   - `BasicOcspResponse` for response data
   - `Asn1OcspUtility` for ASN.1 parsing
   - `readDerEncodedOcspResponse()` and `validateResponse()` functions
   - `SingleResponse` for per-certificate status

6. **SPIFFEValidator** - Alternative SPIFFE/SVID validator

7. **Factory Pattern** - `CertValidatorFactory` for pluggable implementations

The answer file (`/workspace/answer.json`) contains 23 files, 20 key symbols, 10 validation chain functions, and a comprehensive narrative explanation of the entire TLS certificate val

The createStringSanMatcher() factory function creates matchers for DNS, URI, email, IP, and OTHER_NAME SAN types. Matchers support string matching strategies including exact, prefix, suffix, and regex patterns.\\n\\n4. **ContextImpl Classes** (source/common/tls/context_impl.h and .cc): The ContextImpl base class manages TLS contexts and integrates the certificate validator. validation pipeline is implemented across multiple C++ source files in the github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2 repository. The pipeline consists of the following key components:\\n\\n1. **Abstract CertValidator Interface** (source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h): The abstract CertValidator class defines the validation contract with pure virtual methods including addClientValidationContext(), doVerifyCertChain(), and initializeSslContexts(). The ValidationResults struct encapsulates validation status (Pending, Successful, Failed) and detailed error information.\\n\\n2. **DefaultCertValidator Implementation** (source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.h and .cc): This is the primary X.509 certificate validator implementing the CertValidator interface. It performs:\\n   - X.509 chain verification using OpenSSL/BoringSSL\\n   - Certificate hash pinning via verifyCertificateHashList() (SHA-256 DER-encoded)\\n   - SPKI pinning via verifyCertificateSpkiList() (SHA-256 base64-encoded)\\n   - Subject Alternative Name (SAN) verification via verifySubjectAltName() and matchSubjectAltName()\\n   - Subject validation context configuration handling\\n\\n3. **SAN Matcher Components** (source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.h and .cc): The SanMatcher interface and StringSanMatcher implementation handle matching Subject Alternative Names against configured patterns. The createStringSanMatcher() factory function creates matchers for DNS, URI, email, IP, and OTHER_NAME SAN types. Matchers support string matching strategies including exact, prefix, suffix, and regex patterns.\\n\\n4. **ContextImpl Classes** (source/common/tls/context_impl.h and .cc): The ContextImpl base class manages TLS contexts and integrates the certificate validator. It includes:\\n   - TlsContext struct holding SSL_CTX, X.509 certificate chain, and OcspResponseWrapper\\n   - customVerifyCertChain() for asynchronous certificate verification on TCP connections\\n   - customVerifyCertChainForQuic() for QUIC-specific validation\\n   - customVerifyCallback() as the OpenSSL verify callback for custom validation\\n   - Integration with CertValidatorPtr for pluggable validators\\n\\n5. **ServerContextImpl and ClientContextImpl** (source/common/tls/server_context_impl.h/.cc and client_context_impl.h/.cc): Server and client specific context implementations extending ContextImpl, with server context managing OCSP stapling decisions via ocspStapleAction().\\n\\n6. **OCSP Response Parsing and Stapling** (source/common/tls/ocsp/ocsp.h and .cc):\\n   - OcspResponseWrapperImpl: Wraps DER-encoded OCSP responses, created via OcspResponseWrapperImpl::create()\\n   - OcspResponse and BasicOcspResponse: ASN.1 structures for OCSP responses per RFC 6960\\n   - SingleResponse and ResponseData: Structures for individual certificate status information\\n   - Asn1OcspUtility: Parsing utilities for DER-encoded OCSP structures including parseOcspResponse(), parseBasicOcspResponse(), parseResponseData(), parseSingleResponse()\\n   - readDerEncodedOcspResponse() and validateResponse() functions handle OCSP response parsing and validation\\n   - OcspResponseStatus enum for handling OCSP response statuses (Successful, MalformedRequest, InternalError, TryLater, SigRequired, Unauthorized)\\n\\n7. **ASN.1 Parsing Utilities** (source/common/tls/ocsp/asn1_utility.h and .cc): Low-level ASN.1 DER parsing functions supporting OCSP-specific structures.\\n\\n8. **SPIFFEValidator** (source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/cert_validator/spiffe/spiffe_validator.h and .cc): An alternative certificate validator implementing SPIFFE/SVID validation with its own matchSubjectAltName() method for SPIFFE certificate validation.\\n\\n9. **Certificate Factory Pattern** (source/common/tls/cert_validator/factory.h and .cc): CertValidatorFactory interface for registering and creating validator instances, with DefaultCertValidatorFactory as the primary implementation.\\n\\nThe validation chain flows as follows: SSL handshake \u2192 customVerifyCallback() \u2192 ContextImpl::customVerifyCertChain() \u2192 CertValidator::doVerifyCertChain() \u2192 DefaultCertValidator certificate verification methods (including SAN matching via san_matcher.cc) \u2192 OCSP validation (if configured) via OcspResponseWrapperImpl. The pipeline supports both synchronous and asynchronous validation, certificate pinning, OCSP stapling, and extensible SAN matching strategies.\"\n}"

  "text": "The Envoy TLS certificate validation pipeline is implemented across multiple C++ source files in the github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2 repository. The pipeline consists of the following key components:\n\n1. **Abstract CertValidator Interface** (source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h): The abstract CertValidator class defines the validation contract with pure virtual methods including addClientValidationContext(), doVerifyCertChain(), and initializeSslContexts(). The ValidationResults struct encapsulates validation status (Pending, Successful, Failed) and detailed error information.\n\n2. **DefaultCertValidator Implementation** (source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.h and .cc): This is the primary X.509 certificate validator implementing the CertValidator interface. It performs:\n   - X.509 chain verification using OpenSSL/BoringSSL\n   - Certificate hash pinning via verifyCertificateHashList() (SHA-256 DER-encoded)\n   - SPKI pinning via verifyCertificateSpkiList() (SHA-256 base64-encoded)\n   - Subject Alternative Name (SAN) verification via verifySubjectAltName() and matchSubjectAltName()\n   - Subject validation context configuration handling\n\n3. **SAN Matcher Components** (source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.h and .cc): The SanMatcher interface and StringSanMatcher implementation handle matching Subject Alternative Names against configured patterns. The createStringSanMatcher() factory function creates matchers for DNS, URI, email, IP, and OTHER_NAME SAN types. Matchers support string matching strategies including exact, prefix, suffix, and regex patterns.\n\n4. **ContextImpl Classes** (source/common/tls/context_impl.h and .cc): The ContextImpl base class manages TLS contexts and integrates the certificate validator. It includes:\n   - TlsContext struct holding SSL_CTX, X.509 certificate chain, and OcspResponseWrapper\n   - customVerifyCertChain() for asynchronous certificate verification on TCP connections\n   - customVerifyCertChainForQuic() for QUIC-specific validation\n   - customVerifyCallback() as the OpenSSL verify callback for custom validation\n   - Integration with CertValidatorPtr for pluggable validators\n\n5. **ServerContextImpl and ClientContextImpl** (source/common/tls/server_context_impl.h/.cc and client_context_impl.h/.cc): Server and client specific context implementations extending ContextImpl, with server context managing OCSP stapling decisions via ocspStapleAction().\n\n6. **OCSP Response Parsing and Stapling** (source/common/tls/ocsp/ocsp.h and .cc):\n   - OcspResponseWrapperImpl: Wraps DER-encoded OCSP responses, created via OcspResponseWrapperImpl::create()\n   - OcspResponse and BasicOcspResponse: ASN.1 structures for OCSP responses per RFC 6960\n   - SingleResponse and ResponseData: Structures for individual certificate status information\n   - Asn1OcspUtility: Parsing utilities for DER-encoded OCSP structures including parseOcspResponse(), parseBasicOcspResponse(), parseResponseData(), parseSingleResponse()\n   - readDerEncodedOcspResponse() and validateResponse() functions handle OCSP response parsing and validation\n   - OcspResponseStatus enum for handling OCSP response statuses (Successful, MalformedRequest, InternalError, TryLater, SigRequired, Unauthorized)\n\n7. **ASN.1 Parsing Utilities** (source/common/tls/ocsp/asn1_utility.h and .cc): Low-level ASN.1 DER parsing functions supporting OCSP-specific structures.\n\n8. **SPIFFEValidator** (source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/cert_validator/spiffe/spiffe_validator.h and .cc): An alternative certificate validator implementing SPIFFE/SVID validation with its own matchSubjectAltName() method for SPIFFE certificate validation.\n\n9. **Certificate Factory Pattern** (source/common/tls/cert_validator/factory.h and .cc): CertValidatorFactory interface for registering and creating validator instances, with DefaultCertValidatorFactory as the primary implementation.\n\nThe validation chain flows as follows: SSL handshake → customVerifyCallback() → ContextImpl::customVerifyCertChain() → CertValidator::doVerifyCertChain() → DefaultCertValidator certificate verification methods (including SAN matching via san_matcher.cc) → OCSP validation (if configured) via OcspResponseWrapperImpl. The pipeline supports both synchronous and asynchronous validation, certificate pinning, OCSP stapling, and extensible SAN matching strategies."
